An intensely pink, almost violet sky cast its last light onto the dark navy-blue mountains surrounding the valley. The day was dying, sinking into a total and profound silence—it was the hush of a landscape, a region, a world that could be disturbed neither by the bell on a donkey’s neck nor by the fine patter of a flock of sheep passing by the airport barracks.

警察因为我没有签证而拘留了我。但他们无法送我回去，因为我所乘坐的飞机已经起飞，跑道上没有其他飞机。他们在开车进城之前互相商量了一番。我们留下了两个人，机场警卫和我。他身材魁梧，肩膀宽阔，留着无烟煤色的胡须，眼神温柔，脸上挂着不确定而害羞的微笑。他穿着一件长军大衣，带着一支从军队剩余的毛瑟步枪。

The police detained me because I had no visa. But they could not send me back because the plane on which I’d arrived had already flown off and there was no other aircraft on the runway. They conferred among themselves before driving off to town. Two of us remained, the airport guard and I. He was an enormous, broad-shouldered fellow with an anthracite beard, gentle eyes, and an uncertain, shy smile. He wore a long military coat and carried a Mauser rifle from army surplus.

夜色突然降临，天气立刻变冷。我浑身发抖；我是从热带直接飞到这里的，身上只穿了一件衬衫。警卫带来了一些木头、引火物和干草，在一块混凝土板上生火。他把外套递给我，然后用深色骆驼毛毯子把自己裹到眼睛处。我们面对面坐着，一言不发。我们周围什么也没发生。远处，一些蟋蟀醒来了，随后，更远的地方，传来了汽车引擎的轰鸣声。

Night descended suddenly and at once it grew cold. I was trembling; I had flown here straight from the tropics and had only a shirt on my back. The guard brought some wood, kindling, and dry grasses and started a fire on a slab of concrete. He gave me his coat and wrapped himself up to the eyes in a dark camel-hair blanket. We sat facing one another without uttering a word. Nothing was happening around us. Some crickets awoke in the distance and later, farther still, a car engine growled.

早上，警察带着一位老人回来了，他是一位商人，在喀布尔为罗兹的工厂购买棉花。比拉斯先生答应帮忙办理签证；但他并没有答应。他已经在这里呆了一段时间并且有联系。确实，他不仅拿到了签证，还邀请我去他的别墅，很高兴能有一些陪伴。

In the morning the policemen returned with an elderly man, a merchant who bought cotton in Kabul for the factories in Łódz. Mr. Bielas promised to see about a visa; he’d been here for some time already and had connections. Indeed, he not only secured a visa, he also invited me to his villa, pleased to have some company for a while.

喀布尔是尘埃之上。风吹过城市所在的山谷，带来附近沙漠的沙云。空气中悬浮着一种浅棕色、浅灰色的颗粒物，覆盖着一切，渗透到各处，直到风停后才沉降。然后空气变得透明、晶莹剔透。

Kabul is dust upon dust. Winds blow through the valley where the city lies, carrying clouds of sand from the nearby deserts. A pale brown, grayish particulate matter hangs in the air, coating everything, pushing its way in everywhere, settling only when the winds die down. And then the air grows transparent, crystal clear.

每天晚上，街道上都仿佛上演着一场即兴的、即兴的神秘剧。只有路边摊上燃烧的油灯和火把刺破了无边无际的黑暗，它们微弱而摇曳的火焰照亮了摊贩们直接摆在地上、路边、家门口的廉价而微薄的商品。 。在这些行之间灯光下，人们默默地走过——寒冷和风吹拂着弓背、遮盖的身影。

Every evening the streets look as if a spontaneous, improvised mystery play were being staged on them. The all-pervasive darkness is pierced only by oil lamps and torches burning on the street stalls, whose feeble and wavering flames illuminate the cheap and meager goods laid out by the vendors directly on the ground, on patches of road, on the thresholds of houses. Between these rows of lights people pass silently—hunched, covered figures whipped on by the cold and the wind.

当从莫斯科起飞的飞机开始降落在华沙上空时，我的邻居浑身发抖，双手紧紧握住椅子扶手，闭上了眼睛。他的脸灰白、饱经沧桑，布满皱纹。一套发霉的廉价西装宽松地挂在他瘦骨嶙峋的身躯上。我用眼角的余光偷偷地看着他。泪水顺着他的脸颊流下来。过了一会儿，我听到一声压抑但清晰的抽泣声。

When the plane from Moscow started to descend over Warsaw, my neighbor trembled, squeezed the arms of his chair with both hands, and closed his eyes. He had a gray, ravaged face, covered in wrinkles. A musty, cheap suit hung loosely on his thin, bony frame. I looked at him furtively, out of the corner of my eye. Tears were flowing down his cheeks. And a moment later I heard a suppressed but nevertheless distinct sob.

“我很抱歉，”他对我说。 “对不起。但我不相信我会回来。”

“I’m sorry,” he said to me. “I’m sorry. But I didn’t believe that I would return.”

那是 1956 年 12 月，人们仍在从古拉格集中营中走出来。

It was December 1956. People were still coming out of the gulags.

拉比唱奥义书

RABI SINGS THE UPANISHADS

我印度是我第一次与异类相遇，第一次发现新世界。同时，这也是谦卑方面的重要一课。是的，世界教导我们谦卑。我从这次旅程回来，为自己的无知和自己的阅读水平而感到尴尬。那时我意识到现在看来显而易见的事情：一种文化不会仅凭我一挥手就向我揭示它的奥秘；它是一种文化。面对这样的遭遇，我们必须做好充分、详细的准备。

India was my first encounter with otherness, the discovery of a new world. It was at the same time a great lesson in humility. Yes, the world teaches humility. I returned from this journey embarrassed by my own ignorance, at how ill read I was. I realized then what now seems obvious: a culture would not reveal its mysteries to me at a mere wave of my hand; one has to prepare oneself thoroughly and at length for such an encounter.

我对这一课的最初反应，以及对我而言隐含的大量工作的必要性，是跑回家，回到我熟悉的地方，回到我自己的语言，回到已经熟悉的符号和符号的世界。我试图忘记印度，它对我来说意味着我的失败：它的巨大和多样性、它的贫穷和富裕、它的神秘和不可理解已经压垮了我、震惊了我，并最终打败了我。我再次很高兴只在波兰旅行，写下那里的人民，与他们交谈，倾听他们的意见。我们立即相互理解，因共同的经历而团结在一起。

My initial reaction to this lesson, and to the implied necessity of an enormous amount of work on my part, was to run back home, to return to places I knew, to my own language, to the world of already familiar signs and symbols. I tried to forget India, which signified to me my failure: its enormity and diversity, its poverty and riches, its mystery and incomprehensibility had crushed, stunned, and finally defeated me. Once again I was glad to travel only around Poland, write about its people, talk to them, listen to what they had to say. We understood each other instantly, were united by common experience.

但我当然记得印度。波兰的冬天越寒冷，我就越容易想到炎热的喀拉拉邦。夜幕降临得越快，克什米尔耀眼的日出景象就越清晰地浮现出来。世界不再是千篇一律的寒冷和白雪，而是倍增，变得五彩斑斓：既冷又热，雪白又绿，又盛开。

But of course I remembered India. The more bitter the cold of the Polish winter, the more readily I thought of hot Kerala; the quicker darkness fell, the more vividly resurfaced images of Kashmir’s dazzling sunrises. The world was no longer uniformly cold and snowy, but had multiplied, become variegated: it was simultaneously cold and hot, snowy white while also green and blooming.

当我有空闲时间（只有条子，因为报纸上有很多工作）和一些零钱（不幸的是，这是一种更稀有的商品）时，我寻找有关印度的书籍。但我对普通书店和古玩商的探索大多都徒劳无功。在一家旧书店里，我找到了保罗·杜森 (Paul Deussen) 于 1907 年出版的《印度哲学纲要》。德国伟大的印度问题专家、尼采的朋友杜森教授这样解释了印度教哲学的精髓：“这个世界是玛雅的，是幻觉……一切都是虚幻的，除了一个例外，除了我自己的自我，我的阿特曼……[人]感觉自己拥有一切，——所以他不会渴望任何东西，因为他拥有一切可以拥有的东西；——他感觉自己拥有一切，——所以他不会伤害任何东西，因为没有人伤害自己。”

When I had free time (slivers only, as there was much work at the paper) and some spare change (unfortunately, an even rarer commodity), I searched for books about India. But my expeditions to ordinary bookstores and antiquarian dealers ended fruitlessly most often. In one used-book shop I found Outlines of Indian Philosophy, by Paul Deussen, published in 1907. Professor Deussen, a great German specialist on India and friend of Nietzsche’s, thus explained the essence of Hindu philosophy: “This world is mâyâ, is illusion … All is illusive, with one exception, with the exception of my own Self, of my Atman … [man] feels himself everything,—so he will not desire anything, for he has whatever can be had;—he feels himself everything,—so he will not injure anything, for nobody injures himself.”

多伊森谴责欧洲人。他抱怨道，“欧洲人的懒惰试图逃避对印度哲学的研究”——尽管也许“绝望”才是更准确的动机，因为在四千年不间断的发展过程中，这种哲学已经演变成一个体系它是巨大的、不可估量的，足以吓倒和瘫痪除了顽固的冒失鬼和狂热者之外的所有人。此外，在印度教中，深不可测的领域是无边无际的，其中蕴藏着丰富多样的事物，其特点是最令人困惑、相互矛盾和鲜明的对比。这里的一切都以最自然的方式转化为它的对立面，物质事物和神秘现象之间的界限是流动的和转瞬即逝的，一个变成另一个，或者简单地说，永远是另一个；存在转变成虚无，分解并变形为宇宙，变成天体无所不在，变成一种神道，消失在无底的非存在的深处。

Deussen reproaches Europeans. “European idleness,” he complains, “tries to escape the study of Indian philosphy”—though perhaps “despair” is the more accurate motive since, in the course of four thousand years of uninterrupted development, this philosophy has evolved into a system so immense and immeasurable as to intimidate and paralyze all but the hardened daredevil and enthusiast. Furthermore, in Hinduism the sphere of the unfathomable is boundless, and the rich variety of what lies within it is characterized by the most bewildering, mutually contradictory, and stark contrasts. Everything here turns in the most natural way into its opposite, the boundaries between material things and mystical phenomena are fluid and fleeting, one becomes the other or, simply, eternally is the other; being is transformed into nothingness, disintegrates and metamorphoses into the cosmos, into a celestial omnipresence, into a divine way that disappears into the depths of bottomless nonbeing.

印度教有无数的神、神话和信仰，有数百个不同的思想流派、取向和倾向，有数十条救赎之路、美德之路、纯洁实践和禁欲主义规则。印度教的世界是如此之大，以至于它有足够的空间容纳每个人和每件事，相互接受、宽容、和谐和团结。印度教的所有圣书难以统计：仅其中一本《摩诃婆罗多》就有约 22 万首十六音节诗句，是《伊利亚特》和《奥德赛》加起来的八倍！

There is an infinite number of gods, myths, and beliefs in Hinduism, hundreds of the most varied schools of thought, orientations, and tendencies, dozens of roads to salvation, paths of virtue, practices of purity, and rules of asceticism. The world of Hinduism is so great that it has space enough for everyone and everything, for mutual acceptance, tolerance, harmony, and unity. It is impossible to count all the holy books of Hinduism: one of them alone, the Mahabharata, numbers some 220,000 sixteen-syllable verses, which is eight times the Iliad and the Odyssey combined!

有一天，我在一家古书店里发现了瑜伽士拉玛查拉卡 (Yogi Ramacharaka) 于 1905 年出版的一本折角、令人崩溃的著作，书名为《印度瑜伽士呼吸科学：身体、心智、心灵和灵性发展的东方呼吸哲学完整手册》。作者解释说，呼吸是人类最重要的活动，因为我们通过它与世界交流。如果我们停止呼吸，我们就停止了生命。因此，呼吸的质量决定了我们生命的质量，决定了我们是否健康、强壮、智慧。不幸的是，拉马查拉卡说，大多数人，尤其是西方人，呼吸不畅，这就是为什么有这么多疾病、残疾、病弱和抑郁的原因。

One day at an antiquarian bookshop I found a dog-eared, disintegrating work by Yogi Ramacharaka, published in 1905 and entitled The Hindu-Yogi Science of Breath: A Complete Manual of the Oriental Breathing Philosophy of Physical, Mental, Psychic and Spiritual Development. Breathing, explains the author, is the most important activity performed by man, because through it we communicate with the world. If we stop breathing, we stop living. Therefore the quality of our breathing determines the quality of our life, and whether we are healthy, strong, and wise. Unfortunately, says Ramacharaka, most people, especially in the West, breathe poorly, and that is why there is so much disease, disability, sickliness, and depression.

我对培养创造力的练习特别感兴趣，因为我自己在这个目标上遇到了很大的困难。 “平躺在地板或床上，”瑜伽修行者建议，“完全放松，双手轻轻放在太阳神经丛上（胃窝，肋骨开始分开的地方），有节奏地呼吸。当节奏完全建立后，每次吸入都会从宇宙供应中吸收更多的普拉纳或生命能量，这些能量将被神经系统吸收并储存在太阳神经丛中。在每一个呼气将使普拉纳或生命能量分布到全身……”

I was especially interested in the exercises for developing the creative powers, because of my own great difficulties with this objective. “Lying flat on the floor or bed,” the yogi recommended, “completely relaxed, with hands resting lightly over the Solar Plexus (over the pit of the stomach, where the ribs begin to separate), breathe rhythmically. After the rhythm is fully established will that each inhalation will draw in an increased supply of prana or vital energy from the Universal supply, which will be taken up by the nervous system and stored in the Solar Plexus. At each exhalation will that the prana or vital energy is being distributed all over the body….”

我刚读完《印度瑜伽呼吸科学》，罗宾德拉纳特·泰戈尔 (Rabindranath Tagore) 1923 年出版的《孟加拉一瞥》就落入了我的手中。泰戈尔是一位作家、诗人、作曲家和画家。他被比作歌德和让-雅克·卢梭。 1913 年，他被授予诺贝尔文学奖。他写道，当他还是个孩子的时候，小拉比（在家中对他的称呼）是孟加拉婆罗门王室的后裔，他因对父母的服从而表现出色，他在学校的成绩很好，而且他的虔诚堪称典范。他回忆说，早上天还黑的时候，父亲叫醒他，让他背梵文词形变化。过了一会儿，他继续说，天亮了，他的父亲在祈祷后会帮他喝完早上的牛奶。最后，在拉比的陪伴下，他的父亲将再次转向上帝并唱起《奥义书》。

I had barely finished reading The Hindu-Yogi Science of Breath when Glimpses of Bengal by Rabindranath Tagore, published in 1923, fell into my hands. Tagore was a writer, a poet, a composer, and a painter. He was compared to Goethe and Jean-Jacques Rousseau. He was awarded the Nobel Prize for Literature in 1913. When he was a child, little Rabi—as he was called at home—the descendant of a princely family of Bengali Brahmans, distinguished himself, he writes, by his obedience toward his parents, his good grades in school, and his exemplary piety. He recalls that in the morning, while it was still dark, his father woke him to memorize Sanskrit declensions. After a while, he continues, dawn would break, and his father, having said his prayers, would help him finish the morning milk. Finally, with Rabi by his side, his father would turn once more to God and sing the Upanishads.

我试着想象这个场景：黎明时分，父亲和昏昏欲睡的小拉比站在初升的太阳面前，唱着《奥义书》。

I tried to imagine this scene: it is dawning, and the father and small, sleepy Rabi stand facing the rising sun and singing the Upanishads.

《奥义书》是哲学歌曲，其历史可以追溯到三千年前，但仍然充满活力，仍然存在于印度的精神生活中。当我意识到这一点，并想到那个小男孩用《奥义书》中的诗节迎接晨星时，我怀疑我是否能够理解一个孩子们开始唱着哲学诗句的国家。

The Upanishads are philosophical songs dating back three thousand years, but still vibrant, still present in India’s spiritual life. When I realized this, and thought about the small boy greeting the morning star with stanzas from the Upanishads, I doubted whether I could ever comprehend a country in which children start the day singing verses of philosophy.

拉比·泰戈尔是加尔各答的孩子，出生在这座巨大的城市里，下面的事情就发生在我身上。我坐在酒店房间里读希罗多德的书，突然透过窗户听到警报声。我跑到外面。救护车呼啸而过，人们跑进门口避难，一群警察从拐角处冲出来，用长棍殴打逃跑的行人。人们可以闻到煤气和某种东西燃烧的气味。我试图找出发生了什么事。一个手里拿着石头跑过的人喊道：“语言战！”并继续前进。语言战争！我不知道细节，但很早就知道，语言冲突在这个国家可能会采取暴力和血腥的形式：示威、街头冲突、谋杀，甚至自焚行为。

Rabi Tagore was a child of Calcutta, born in that monstrously huge city in which the following thing happened to me. I was sitting in a hotel room reading Herodotus when through the window I heard the wailing of sirens. I ran outside. Ambulances were screeching by, people were running into doorways to shelter, a group of policemen burst out from around a corner, thrashing the fleeing pedestrians with long sticks. One could smell the odor of gas and of something burning. I tried to find out what was going on. A man sprinting by with a stone in his hand yelled, “Language war!” and rushed on. Language war! I did not know the details, but had been made aware earlier that linguistic conflicts could assume violent and bloody forms in this country: demonstrations, street clashes, murders, even acts of self-immolation.

只有到了印度，我才意识到我不懂英语是没有意义的——因为这里只有精英人才会说英语。不到总人口的2%！其余的人讲的是其他几十种语言中的一种。从这个意义上说，我不懂英语让我感觉更接近、更接近我所经过的城市里的普通人或村庄里的农民。我们是同一条船——我和五亿印度居民！

Only in India did I realize that my unfamiliarity with English was meaningless—insofar as only the elite spoke it here. Less than 2 percent of the population! The rest spoke one of the dozens of other languages. In this sense, my not knowing English helped me feel closer, more akin to the ordinary folk in the cities or the peasants in the villages I passed. We were in the same boat—I and half a billion of India’s inhabitants!

虽然这个想法给了我安慰，但它也困扰着我——我想知道，为什么我会因为不懂英语而感到尴尬，而不是因为我不懂印地语、孟加拉语、古吉拉特语、泰卢固语、乌尔都语、泰米尔语、旁遮普语或这个国家还使用其他许多语言吗？可及性的争论是无关紧要的：当时学习英语就像学习印地语或孟加拉语一样稀有。那么我这是欧洲中心主义吗？我是否认为欧洲语言比我当时作为客人的这个国家的语言更重要？认为英语优越是对印度教徒尊严的冒犯，对他们来说，与母语的关系是一个微妙而重要的问题。他们准备为了捍卫自己的语言而献出自己的生命，并在柴堆上焚烧。这种热情和决心源于这样一个事实：这里的身份是由一个人所说的语言决定的。例如，孟加拉人是指母语是孟加拉语的人。语言是一个人的身份证，甚至是一个人的面孔和灵魂。这就是为什么完全不同的事情上的冲突——例如社会和宗教问题——可以采取语言战争的形式。

While this thought gave me comfort, it also troubled me—why, I wondered, am I embarrassed that I don’t know English but not that I don’t know Hindi, Bengali, Gujarati, Telugu, Urdu, Tamil, Punjabi, or any of the many other languages spoken in this country? The argument of accessibility was irrelevant: the study of English was at the time as rare a thing as that of Hindi or Bengali. So was this Eurocentrism on my part? Did I believe a European language to be more important than those languages of this country in which I was then a guest? Deeming English superior was an offense to the dignity of Hindus, for whom the relationship to their native languages was a delicate and important matter. They were prepared to give up their lives in the defense of their language, to burn on a pyre. This fervor and resolve stemmed from the fact that identity here is determined by the language one speaks. A Bengali, for example, is someone whose mother tongue is Bengali. Language is one’s identity card, one’s face and soul, even. Which is why conflicts about something else entirely—about social and religious issues, for instance—can assume the form of language wars.

在搜索有关印度的书籍时，我会询问是否有关于希罗多德的内容。希罗多德开始引起我的兴趣——事实上，我完全喜欢上了他。我很感激他在印度的不确定和困惑时刻陪伴在我身边，帮助我完成他的书。从他的写作方式来看，他似乎是一个待人友善、对世界充满好奇的人。他总是有很多问题，并准备好长途跋涉数千公里来寻找其中任何一个问题的答案。

Searching for books on India, I would ask if there was anything about Herodotus. Herodotus had started to interest me—I took a downright fancy to him, in fact. I was grateful for his being by my side in India during moments of uncertainty and confusion, for helping me with his book. Judging by how he wrote, he seemed a man kindly disposed toward others and curious about the world. Someone who always had many questions and was ready to wander thousands of kilometers to find an answer to any one of them.

然而，当我沉浸在各种资料中时，我发现我们对希罗多德的生平知之甚少，而且即使我们掌握的少数事实也并不完全可靠。因为与罗宾德拉纳特·泰戈尔（或者，例如，他同时代的马塞尔·普鲁斯特，两人都仔细地剖析了他们童年的每一个细节）相比，希罗多德和这个时代的其他伟人——苏格拉底、伯里克利、索福克勒斯——几乎没有告诉我们什么关于他的。难道不是习惯吗？童年是否被认为无关紧要？希罗多德只说他来自哈利卡纳苏斯。哈利卡纳苏斯坐落在一个形状像圆形剧场的平静海湾之上，位于世界上一个美丽的地方，亚洲西岸与地中海的交汇处。这是一片阳光、温暖、光明、橄榄树和葡萄园的土地。人们本能地觉得，出生在这里的人，必然拥有一颗善良的心、开阔的胸怀、健康的身体、始终如一的开朗性格。

When I immersed myself in various sources, however, I learned that we know little about Herodotus’s life, and that even the few facts we do have are not entirely reliable. For in contrast to Rabindranath Tagore—or, for instance, his contemporary Marcel Proust, both of whom meticulously parsed every detail of their childhoods—Herodotus, like the other great men of this epoch—Socrates, Pericles, Sophocles—tells us next to nothing about his. Was it not customary? Was childhood considered irrelevant? Herodotus says only that he came from Halicarnassus. Halicarnassus lies above a calm bay shaped like an amphitheater, in a beautiful part of the world, where the western shore of Asia meets the Mediterranean Sea. It is a land of sun, warmth, and light, of olive trees and vineyards. One instinctively feels that someone born here must naturally have a good heart, an open mind, a healthy body, a consistently cheerful disposition.

传记作者倾向于认为希罗多德出生于公元前490 年至 480 年之间，也许是 485 年。这些是世界文化史上非常重要的年份。公元前480年左右，佛陀出发前往另一个世界；一年后，鲁国，孔子死亡；五十年后，柏拉图出生。亚洲是世界的中心；即使就希腊人而言，他们社会中最有创造力的成员——爱奥尼亚人——也生活在亚洲。欧洲还没有存在；它仅作为神话存在，以美丽的女孩欧罗巴（Europa）的名义存在，欧罗巴是腓尼基国王阿革诺尔（Agenor）的女儿，宙斯将她变成一头白牛，将她带到克里特岛与她为所欲为。

Biographers tend to agree that Herodotus was born between 490 and 480 B.C.E., perhaps in 485. These are greatly important years in the history of world culture. Around 480 B.C.E., Buddha departs for the other world; a year later, in the Lu principality, Confucius dies; Plato will be born fifty years later. Asia is the center of the world; even insofar as the Greeks are concerned, the most creative members of their society—the Ionians—also live in Asia. There is no Europe yet; it exists as myth only, in the name of a beautiful girl, Europa, daughter of the Phoenician king Agenor, whom Zeus, transformed into a white bull, will carry off to Crete to have his way with her.

希罗多德的父母？他的兄弟姐妹？他的房子？所有这一切都处于深深的阴影地带的不确定性之中。哈利卡纳苏斯是希腊殖民地，土地上受波斯人管辖，居住着非希腊本土居民——卡里安人。他的父亲名叫莱克西斯，这不是希腊名字，所以他可能是卡里安人。他的母亲很可能是希腊人。因此，希罗多德是希腊卡里安人，一个混血儿。这些在不同文化中成长的人，作为不同血统的混合体，他们的世界观是由边界、距离、差异、多样性等概念决定的。我们遇到了各种各样的人，从狂热、激烈的宗派主义者，到消极、冷漠的乡下人，再到开放、包容的流浪者——世界公民。这取决于他们的血液如何混合，其中的灵魂如何定居。

The parents of Herodotus? His siblings? His house? All of this is in deep shadowland uncertainty. Halicarnassus was a Greek colony on land subject to the Persians, with a non-Greek native population—the Carians. His father was called Lyxes, which is not a Greek name, so perhaps he was a Carian. It was his mother who most probably was Greek. Herodotus was therefore a Greek Carian, an ethnic half-breed. Such people who grow up amid different cultures, as a blend of different bloodlines, have their worldview determined by such concepts as border, distance, difference, diversity. We encounter the widest array of human types among them, from fanatical, fierce sectarians, to passive, apathetic provincials, to open, receptive wanderers—citizens of the world. It depends on how their blood got mixed, what spirits settled in it.

希罗多德是一个什么样的孩子？他是对每个人微笑并自愿伸出手，还是闷闷不乐地躲在母亲的衣服褶皱里？他是不是一个永远的爱哭鬼、爱发牢骚的人，时不时让他饱受折磨的母亲感叹：天哪，我为什么生出这样一个孩子！还是他很开朗，向四周传播欢乐？他是听话、有礼貌，还是用问题折磨每个人：太阳从哪里来？为什么它那么高，没人能够到呢？为什么它会隐藏在海底？难道就不怕淹死吗？

What sort of child is Herodotus? Does he smile at everyone and willingly extend his hand, or does he sulk and hide in the folds of his mother’s garments? Is he an eternal crybaby and whiner, giving his tormented mother at times to sigh: Gods, why did I give birth to such a child! Or is he cheerful, spreading joy all around? Is he obedient and polite, or does he torture everyone with questions: Where does the sun come from? Why is it so high up that no one can reach it? Why does it hide beneath the sea? Isn’t it afraid of drowning?

那么在学校呢？他和谁共用一张长凳？作为惩罚，他们是否让他坐在某个不守规矩的男孩旁边？或者，众神禁止，一个女孩？他学在泥板上写字是不是很快？他经常迟到吗？他上课时会扭动吗？他会向其他人隐瞒答案吗？他是个爱说闲话的人吗？

And in school? With whom does he share a bench? Did they seat him, as punishment, next to some unruly boy? Or, the gods forbid, a girl? Did he learn quickly to write on the clay tablet? Is he often late? Does he squirm during lessons? Does he slip others the answers? Is he a tattletale?

还有玩具？生活在两半千年前的小希腊人在玩什么？用木头雕刻的踏板车？他在海边建造了沙堡吗？爬树？让自己变成粘土鸟、鱼和马，我们今天可以在博物馆里研究它们？

And toys? What did a little Greek living two and a half thousand years ago play with? A scooter carved out of wood? Did he build sand castles at the edge of the sea? Climb trees? Make himself clay birds, fish, and horses, which we can study today in museums?

他童年的哪些方面将终生铭记？对于小拉比来说，最崇高的时刻就是在父亲身边做晨祷。对于小马塞尔来说，他正在黑暗的房间里等待妈妈过来拥抱他晚安。小希罗多德以这种方式预见到了什么样的经历？

Which aspects of his childhood will he remember for the rest of his life? For little Rabi, the most exalted moment was the morning prayer at his father’s side. For little Marcel, it was waiting in a dark room for his mother to come and hug him good night. Which experience did little Herodotus anticipate in this way?

他的父亲做了什么？哈利卡纳苏斯是一个港口小镇，位于亚洲、近东和希腊本土之间的贸易路线上。来自西西里岛和意大利的腓尼基商船、来自比雷埃夫斯和阿尔戈斯的希腊商船以及来自利比亚和尼罗河三角洲的埃及商船也曾在此停靠。希罗多德的父亲本人可能也是一名商人吗？也许是他点燃了儿子对世界的好奇心。他是否曾一次从家里消失数周甚至数月，让他的妻子在孩子的询问下回答“父亲在……”？在这里，人们可以想象一系列地名，他从中吸取了教训——在遥远的某个地方，存在着一个无所不能的世界，它可以永远把他的父亲从他身边带走，但也可以（感谢诸神！）把他带去。再次回来。认识这个世界的诱惑就是这样诞生的吗？诱惑和决心？

What did his father do? Halicarnassus was a small port town lying on the trade route between Asia, the Near East, and Greece proper. Phoenician merchant ships from Sicily and Italy stopped here, as did Greek ships from Piraeus and Argos, and Egyptian ones from Libya and the Nile delta. Might Herodotus’s father have been a merchant himself? Perhaps it was he who kindled in his son a curiosity about the world. Did he disappear from home for weeks and months at a time, leaving his wife, questioned by her child, to answer that “Father is in …”? And here one can imagine a list of place-names from which he drew one lesson—that somewhere, far away, there exists an omnipotent world which could take his father away from him forever, but also (thank the gods!) can bring him back again. Is that how the temptation to get to know this world was born? The temptation and the resolve?

从我们掌握的少数事实中，我们知道小希罗多德有一个叔叔，姓潘亚西斯，他是各种诗歌和史诗的作者。这位叔叔是否可能带他去散步，教导他诗歌之美、修辞奥秘、讲故事的艺术？因为历史是这是天赋的产物，也是写作技巧和技术掌握的典范。

From the few facts that have reached us, we know that little Herodotus had an uncle whose last name was Panyassis, and that he was the author of various poems and epics. Did this uncle perhaps take him on walks, instruct him in the beauties of poetry, the arcana of rhetoric, the art of storytelling? Because The Histories is the product of natural talent but also an example of writerly craft, of technical mastery.

当希罗多德还是个年轻人时——这似乎是他一生中第一次也是唯一一次——多亏了他的父亲和叔叔，他们参与了反对哈利卡纳苏斯暴君吕格达米斯的叛乱，希罗多德就卷入了政治。暴君成功镇压了叛乱。叛变者在萨摩斯岛上避难，这是一座山岛，向西北划了两天船。希罗多德在这里度过了数年，也许他就是从这里出发环游世界的。即使他偶尔出现在哈利卡纳苏斯，也只是短暂的。他这么做是为了什么？去看他的母亲？我们不知道。人们大概可以假设他没有再回到这里。

While still a young man—and it seems for the first and only time in his life—Herodotus gets embroiled in politics, thanks to his father and uncle, who take part in the revolt against the tyrant of Halicarnassus, Lygdamis. The tyrant succeeds in suppressing the rebellion. The mutineers take refuge on Samos, a mountainous island two days of rowing to the northwest. Herodotus spends years here, and perhaps it is from here that he sets forth around the world. If he reappears now and then in Halicarnassus, it is only briefly. What would he do that for? To see his mother? We do not know. One can probably assume that he did not return here again.

这是公元前五世纪中叶；希罗多德抵达雅典。船抵达雅典比雷埃夫斯港；从这里到雅典卫城有八公里，这段距离需要骑马，或者像往常一样步行。雅典当时是一个世界大都市，地球上最重要的城市。希罗多德是外省人，不是雅典人，因此有点外国人的味道，虽然这些人受到的待遇比奴隶好，但他们的待遇不如本土雅典人。雅典社会对种族高度敏感，具有强烈的优越感、排他感，甚至傲慢感。

It is the middle of the fifth century B.C.E.; Herodotus arrives in Athens. The ship reaches the Athenian port of Piraeus; it is eight kilometers from here to the Acropolis, a distance traversed on horseback or, as was often the case, on foot. Athens is then a world metropolis, the most important city on the planet. Herodotus is provincial, a non-Athenian, and thus something of a foreigner, and while such individuals are treated better than slaves, they are not treated as well as native Athenians. Athenian society was highly sensitive to race, with a strongly developed sense of superiority, exclusivity, arrogance even.

但希罗多德似乎很快就适应了他的新城市。这位三十多岁的男人性格开朗，友善，是一个很好相处的人。他演讲、参加会议、作家之夜——他可能就是这样谋生的。他与苏格拉底、索福克勒斯、伯里克利建立了重要的联系。这并没有那么困难。那时的雅典，人口十万，面积并不大，而且建筑严密，甚至有些混乱。只有两个地方脱颖而出：宗教崇拜的中心——雅典卫城，以及会议、活动、商业、政治和社会生活的中心——集市。人们从清晨就聚集在这里。集市广场总是人头攒动，充满生机。我们肯定也会在这里找到希罗多德。但他并没有在这座城市停留太久。大约在他抵达时，雅典当局通过了一项严厉的法律，根据该法律，只有父母都出生在紧邻雅典的阿提卡地区的人才有权享有政治权利。希罗多德无法获得雅典公民身份。他再次出发，最终在意大利南部的希腊殖民地图里永久定居。

But it appears that Herodotus adapts quickly to his new city. The thirty-something-year-old man is open, friendly, a hail-fellow-well-met. He gives lectures, appears for meetings, author evenings—he probably makes his living that way. He establishes important contacts—with Socrates, Sophocles, Pericles. This isn’t that difficult. Athens, with a population of one hundred thousand, isn’t large in those days, and is tightly, even chaotically built up. Two places only stand out and distinguish themselves: the center of religious cults, the Acropolis, and the center of meetings, events, commerce, politics, and social life—the Agora. People gather here from the early morning. The square of the Agora is always crowded, full of life. We would surely find Herodotus here as well. But he does not stay in the city for long. At approximately the time of his arrival, Athenian authorities pass a draconian law, according to which only those both of whose parents were born in Attica, the region immediately surrounding Athens, are entitled to political rights. Herodotus is unable to obtain Athenian citizenship. He sets off once again, and finally settles permanently in southern Italy, in the Greek colony of Thurii.

对于后来发生的事情，意见不一。有些人相信他再也没有离开过那里。其他人则声称他后来再次访问了希腊，有人在雅典看到了他。甚至还提到了马其顿。但事实上，没有什么是确定的。他也许在六十岁就去世了——但是死在哪里呢？什么情况下？他是否在图里伊度过了最后的岁月，坐在梧桐树荫下写书？或者也许他看不清而把它口授给抄写员？他有笔记吗？还是只能依靠记忆？那个时代的人们记忆力很强。他很可能记得克洛伊索斯和巴比伦、大流士和斯基泰人、波斯人、塞莫皮莱和萨拉米斯的故事。以及构成《历史》的许多其他故事。

Opinion differs as to what happens later. Some believe that he did not budge from there again. Others claim that he later visited Greece once more, that he was sighted in Athens. Even Macedonia is mentioned. But in point of fact nothing is certain. He dies at age sixty, perhaps—but where? Under what circumstances? Did he spend his last years in Thurii, sitting in the shade of a sycamore tree and writing his book? Or maybe he could no longer see well enough and dictated it to a scribe? Did he have notes or was he able to rely on memory alone? People in those days had great powers of recall. He could well have remembered the stories of Croesus and Babylon, of Darius and the Scythians, of Persians, Thermopylae, and Salamis. And so many of the other tales that constitute The Histories.

或者希罗多德可能死在一艘横渡地中海某处的船上？又或许他正沿着路走，坐在一块石头上休息，就再也没有起来？希罗多德消失了，在二十五个世纪前的某个无法精确确定的年份和我们不知道的地方离开了我们。

Or perhaps Herodotus dies on board a ship sailing somewhere across the Mediterranean? Or perhaps he is walking along a road and sits down on a stone to rest, never to get up again? Herodotus vanishes, leaves us twenty-five centuries ago in a year that is impossible to pinpoint precisely and in a place we do not know.

报社。

The newspaper office.

实地考察。

Field trips.

大会。会议。对话。

Assemblies. Meetings. Conversations.

在空闲的时候，我坐在字典（一本正宗的英文字典终于出版了）和各种有关印度的书籍中（贾瓦哈拉尔·尼赫鲁的宏伟著作《发现印度》刚刚出版，圣雄甘地的伟大自传，以及美丽的Panchatantra，或印度的智慧，五本书。斯大林去世后，审查制度放松了，多年来一直被锁在钥匙里的书籍开始出现）。

In my free moments I sit amidst dictionaries (a proper English one has finally been published) and various books about India (the imposing work of Jawaharlal Nehru, The Discovery of India, has just come out, the great autobiography of Mahatma Gandhi, and the beautiful Panchatantra, or the Wisdom of India, Five Books. After Stalin’s death, censorship had eased and books that for years had been kept under lock and key started to appear).

每读到一本新书，我都感觉自己正在踏上一次新的印度之旅，回忆我去过的地方，发现一些我之前以为自己知道的事物的新深度和方面、新含义。这些旅程比我原来的旅程更加多维。我还发现，通过阅读更多书籍、研究地图、观看绘画和照片，这些探险活动可以进一步延长、重复和增强。更重要的是，它们比实际旅行有一定的优势——在像这样的图像旅行中，可以随时停下来，冷静地观察，倒带到上一个图像等等，这是真实旅行中所具备的。既没有时间，也没有机会。

With each new title I read, I felt as if I were undertaking a new journey to India, recalling places I had visited and discovering new depths and aspects, fresh meanings, of things which earlier I had assumed I knew. These journeys were much more multidimensional than my original one. I discovered also that these expeditions could be further prolonged, repeated, augmented by reading more books, studying maps, looking at paintings and photographs. What is more, they had a certain advantage over the actual trip—in an iconographic journey such as this, one could stop at any point, calmly observe, rewind to the previous image, etc., something for which on a real journey there is neither the time nor the chance.

所以我在这里，越来越全神贯注于印度的非凡和财富，认为随着时间的推移，这个国家将成为我的主题祖国，当 1957 年秋天的一天，我们全知的秘书 Krysia Korta 将我从我的办公室叫出来。报纸上的人神色神秘、焦躁，低声对我说：

So here I am, becoming increasingly engrossed in India’s extraor-dinariness and riches, thinking that with time this country will become my thematic homeland, when one day in the fall of 1957 our omniscient secretary, Krysia Korta, called me out of my office at the newspaper and, looking mysterious, agitated, whispered to me:

“你要去中国。”

“You’re going to China.”

毛主席的

一百朵花

CHAIRMAN MAO’S

ONE HUNDRED FLOWERS

1957年秋

Autumn 1957

我步行到达中国。嗯，我经阿姆斯特丹和东京飞往香港。在香港，一列当地火车把我带到了一个空旷的小车站——有人告诉我，在那里我可以进入中国。然而实际上，当我走上站台时，只有一名售票员和一名警察走近，他们指着远处地平线上的一座桥。 “中国！”警察说道。

I reached China on foot. Well, I flew to Hong Kong via Amsterdam and Tokyo. In Hong Kong, a local train took me to a small station in an open field—where, I had been told, I would be able to cross into China. In reality, however, when I stepped down onto the platform, it was only to be approached by a conductor and a policeman, who gestured toward a bridge on the far horizon. “China!” the policeman said.

他是一名穿着英国警察制服的中国男子。他陪我沿着柏油路走了一段路，然后祝我一路顺利，然后返回车站。我一个人继续前行，一手提着行李箱，一手提着一袋书。太阳无情地照着，空气又闷又热，苍蝇嗡嗡地飞来飞去。

He was a Chinese man in a British police uniform. He walked with me a ways along the asphalt road, then wished me a good journey and turned back for the station. I continued on alone, carrying my suitcase in one hand and a bag full of books in the other. The sun beat down mercilessly, the air was hot and heavy, flies buzzed aggressively.

桥很短，有一个对角的金属格栅，下面流着一条半干涸的河流。再往前，矗立着一扇高高的大门，上面开满了鲜花，上面有中文标志，上面有一个徽章——一个红色的盾牌和五颗黄色的星星，四颗小一颗大。守卫站在大门附近。他们仔细检查了我的护照，把相关数据记在一个大账本上，然后让我继续走——走向大约半公里外可见的火车。我在炎热的天气里艰难地走着，汗流浃背，周围是成群的苍蝇。

The bridge was short, with a diagonal metal grating, and below it flowed a half dried-up river. Further on stood a tall gate covered in flowers, with signs in Chinese and on top a coat of arms—a red shield and five yellow stars, four small and one large. Guards stood near the gate. They carefully inspected my passport, wrote the relevant data down in a big ledger, and told me to keep walking—toward a train which was visible perhaps half a kilometer away. I walked on in the heat, with great effort, perspiring, amidst swarms of flies.

火车上空无一人。这些车厢与从香港出发的火车上的车厢类似——座位成排排列，没有单独的车厢。终于，我们上路了。我们走过的风景阳光明媚，绿意盎然，从窗户吹进来的空气温暖湿润，有热带的味道。这一切都让我想起了印度，马德拉斯和本地治里周边地区的印度。通过这些次大陆的类比，我开始有宾至如归的感觉。我置身于我熟悉和喜欢的风景之中。火车经常停站，小站上车的人也越来越多。他们穿着相似，男人穿着深蓝色牛仔夹克，扣子一直扣到下巴，女人穿着同样剪裁的花裙子。他们坐得挺直，面朝前方，一言不发。

The train was empty. The cars resembled those on the train from Hong Kong—seats arranged in rows, no separate compartments. Finally, we were on our way. The landscape we traversed was sunny and green, the air coming in through the windows felt warm and humid and smelled of the tropics. It all reminded me of India, the India from the area around Madras and Pondicherry. Through these subcontinental analogies, I began to feel at home. I was among landscapes I knew and liked. The train stopped frequently and more and more people got on at the little stations. They were dressed alike, the men in dark blue denim jackets buttoned up to their chins, the women in flowery dresses identically cut. They sat straight-backed, silent, facing forward.

在其中一个车站，当火车已经满员时，三个穿着亮靛蓝色制服的人上了车——一名年轻女子和她的两名男助手。女孩用果断、洪亮的声音发表了一段相当长的演讲，随后其中一个男人给每个人递了一杯杯子，另一个男人从金属壶里倒了绿茶。茶是热的；乘客们对着它吹气以使其冷却，然后大声地喝了一小口。除此之外，沉默仍在继续。没有人说过一句话。我试图读懂乘客们的表情，但他们都僵住了，看上去没有任何表情。另外，我不想太仔细地审视它们，因为担心这会被认为是粗鲁的，甚至可能会引起怀疑。当然没有人在看我，尽管在所有这些工作夹克和华丽的密布大衣中，我穿着一年前在罗马购买的优雅的意大利西装一定显得很奇怪。

At one of the stations, when the train was already full, three people in uniforms of bright indigo came on board—a young woman and her two male helpers. The girl delivered a rather long speech in a decisive stentorian voice, after which one of the men handed everyone a cup and the second one poured out green tea from a metal pot. The tea was hot; the passengers blew on it to cool it and drank in small gulps, slurping loudly. Other than that, the silence continued. No one spoke so much as a word. I tried reading the passengers’ faces, but they were frozen, seemingly without expression. Plus, I didn’t want to scrutinize them too intently, for fear that this would be deemed rude or perhaps even arouse suspicion. Certainly no one was looking at me, although among all these work jackets and flowery percales I must have cut quite a queer figure in my elegant Italian suit purchased a year earlier in Rome.

经过三天的旅程，我到达了北京。天气很冷，一阵寒冷干燥的风吹来，将这座城市和居民笼罩在寒冷的空气中。灰色的尘埃云。青年报《中国》的两名记者在灯光微弱的车站等我。我们握手，其中一个人僵硬地站着，几乎立正，大声说道：

I reached Peking after a three-day journey. It was cold and a chill dry wind was blowing, covering the city and its inhabitants in clouds of gray dust. Two journalists from the youth newspaper Chungkuo were waiting for me at the barely illuminated station. We shook hands, and one of them, standing stiffly, almost at attention, declaimed:

“我们对你们的到来感到高兴，因为这证明了毛主席宣布的百花政治正在取得成果。毛主席建议我们要与他人合作，分享经验，这正是我们各自编辑部交换常驻通讯员的做法。我们作为《青年旗帜报》驻北京的常驻通讯员向您致意，作为交换，我们自己的常驻通讯员将在适当的时候前往华沙。”

“We are pleased about your arrival because it is proof that the politics of One Hundred Flowers, announced by Chairman Mao, is bearing fruit. Chairman Mao recommends that we collaborate with others and share our experiences, and that is precisely what our respective editorial offices are doing in exchanging their permanent correspondents. We greet you as the permanent correspondent of Sztandar Młodych (The Banner of Youth) in Peking, and in exchange our own permanent correspondent will, at the appropriate time, travel to Warsaw.”

我听着，冻得浑身发抖，因为我既没有夹克，也没有外套，徒劳地四处寻找温暖的地方。最后，我们挤进一辆 Pobieda 车，驱车前往酒店。在那里迎接我们的是一位中国记者向我介绍的人，他是李同志。他们解释说，他将成为我的永久翻译。我们都互相说俄语，从现在开始，俄语就是我在中国的语言。

I listened, trembling from the cold, for I had neither a jacket nor a coat, and looked about in vain for someplace warm. Finally we piled into a Pobieda and drove to the hotel. We were met there by a man whom the reporters from Chungkuo introduced to me as Comrade Li. He was to be my permanent translator, they explained. We all spoke Russian to one another, which from now on would be my language in China.

我的设想是这样的：我会在一栋小房子里租一个房间，这些小房子隐藏在沿着北京街道绵延不绝的粘土或沙墙后面。房间里有一张桌子、两把椅子、一张床、一个衣橱、一个书架、一台打字机和一部电话。我会参观《中国》的编辑部，获取新闻、阅读、实地考察、收集信息、撰写和发送文章，当然，同时也学习中文。我会参观博物馆、图书馆和建筑古迹，会见教授和作家，一般来说，会在乡村和城市、商店和学校遇到无数有趣的人；去大学、市场、工厂；到佛教寺庙和党委，以及其他数十个值得了解和调查的地方。中国是一个幅员辽阔的国家，我告诉自己，欣喜地想到，除了作为记者和记者的工作之外，我还有机会收集无数的印象和经历，有一天我离开这里时，会被新的见解、发现、知识所丰富。 。

Here is how I had imagined it: I would get a room in one of the little houses hidden behind the clay or sand walls that stretched without end along Peking’s streets. There would be a table in the room, two chairs, a bed, an armoire, a bookshelf, a typewriter, and a telephone. I would visit the editorial offices of Chungkuo, get the news, read, go out into the field, gather information, write and send articles, and all the while, of course, study Chinese. I would visit museums, libraries, and architectural monuments, meet professors and writers, in general encounter countless interesting people in villages and in cities, in shops and in schools; go to the university, to the marketplace, and to the factory; to Buddhist temples and to Party committees—and to dozens of other places worth knowing and investigating. China is an immense country, I told myself, joyfully thinking that besides my work as a correspondent and reporter I would have the opportunity to gather an infinite number of impressions and experiences, one day to depart from here enriched by new insights, discoveries, knowledge.

我满怀厚望，跟着李同志上楼到了我的房间，而他则从我的大厅对面进入了一间房间。我去关门，这时注意到它既没有门把手，也没有锁，而且，它的铰链的位置迫使门永远向走廊保持打开状态。我还注意到，李同志的房间门同样半开着，让他时刻注视着我。

Full of these high hopes, I followed Comrade Li upstairs to my room, while he entered one directly across the hall from mine. I went to close my door and at that moment noticed that it had neither doorknob nor lock, and, moreover, that its hinges were so positioned as to force the door to remain permanently open onto the hallway. I noted, too, that the door to Comrade Li’s room was similarly ajar and allowing him always to keep an eye on me.

我假装什么也没注意到，开始打开我的书包。我拿出包里最上面的《希罗多德》，然后是三卷《毛泽东选集》、《庄子的南花真经》，还有几本在香港买的《中国怎么了》，作者：罗德尼·吉尔伯特；《中国近代史》，作者：KS Latourette；刘无极《儒家哲学简史》 ；亚洲的起义；莉莉·阿贝格的《东亚思想》；还有汉语课本和词典，我决定立即开始学习。

I pretended not to notice anything and started to unpack my books. I took out Herodotus, near the top in my bag, then three volumes of the Selected Works of Mao Tse-tung, The True Classic of Southern Florescence by Chuang Tzu, and several titles I had purchased in Hong Kong: What’s Wrong with China, by Rodney Gilbert; A History of Modern China, by K. S. Latourette; A Short History of Confucian Philosophy, by Liu Wu-chi; The Revolt of Asia; The Mind of East Asia, by Lily Abegg; as well as textbooks and dictionaries of the Chinese language, which I decided to start learning at once.

第二天一早，李同志带我去了《中国》编辑部。我第一次看到北京的白天。四面八方都是隐藏在墙后的低矮房屋的海洋。墙壁上方突出了深灰色屋顶的顶部，屋顶的尖端像翅膀一样向上卷曲。从远处看，它们就像一大群一动不动的黑鸟，等待着起飞的信号。

The following morning Comrade Li took me to Chungkuo’s editorial offices. For the first time I saw Peking by day. In every direction stretched a sea of low houses hidden behind walls. Above the walls protruded the tops of dark-gray roofs, whose tips curled upward like wings. From a distance they resembled a gigantic flock of motionless black birds awaiting the signal to take flight.

我在报纸上受到了热烈的欢迎。主编是个又高又瘦的年轻人，他说很高兴我的到来，这样我们就共同实现了毛主席的嘱咐——让百花齐放！

I was given a warm welcome at the paper. The editor in chief, a tall, thin young man, said that he was happy at my arrival, for in this way we jointly fulfilled Chairman Mao’s prescription—let a hundred flowers bloom!

我回答说，我也很高兴来到这里，我知道等待着我的任务，我想补充一点，我打算在空闲时间学习《毛泽东选集》 ，我我带来了三卷本。

I answered that I, too, was very glad to be here, that I was aware of the tasks awaiting me, and that I wished to add that in my free time I intended to study the Selected Works of Mao Tse-tung, which I had brought with me in a three-volume edition.

这得到了极大的满意和认可。事实上，我们喝着绿茶的整个谈话，都归结为这种寒暄，以及对毛主席和他的百花政治的赞扬。

This was greeted with great satisfaction and approval. The entire conversation, in fact, throughout which we also sipped green tea, came down to such exchanges of pleasantries, as well as to praising Chairman Mao and his politics of One Hundred Flowers.

过了一会儿，主人们突然沉默了，就像遵照命令一样。李同志站起来看着我，我感觉到这次访问已经结束了。每个人都张开双臂、面带微笑，热情地告别。

After a while, my hosts suddenly fell silent, as if following an order. Comrade Li rose and looked at me—I sensed that the visit was at an end. Everyone said his farewells with great warmth, smiling and with wide open arms.

整个访问的安排和进行，在其过程中一无所获——没有触及任何具体主题，更不用说讨论了。他们没有问我任何问题，也没有给我机会询问我的逗留和工作将如何安排。

The entire visit was arranged and conducted in such a fashion as to accomplish nothing in its course—not one single concrete subject was touched upon, let alone discussed. They had asked me nothing and had given me no opportunity to inquire how my sojourn and my work were to be structured.

但是，我推断，也许这就是当地的习俗。也许快速进入正题被认为是不礼貌的？我当然不止一次地读到，在东方，生活节奏比我们西方人习惯的要慢，凡事都有定时，必须冷静和耐心，必须学会等待、成长内心平静、平静，认为道不重动而重静，不重动而重闲，所有的急躁、激情和狂乱在这里都会引起厌恶，并被解释为不良教养和缺乏修养的症状。

But, I reasoned, perhaps such are local customs. Perhaps it is considered impolite to get to the point quickly? I had certainly read, more than once, that in the East the rhythm of life is slower than what we westerners are used to, that there is a time for everything, that one must be calm and patient, one must learn to wait, grow internally calm and tranquil, that the Tao values not motion but stillness, not activity but idleness, and that all haste, passion, and frenzy arouse distaste here and are interpreted as symptoms of bad upbringing and a lack of refinement.

我也深知，在幅员辽阔的中国面前，我只是一粒尘埃，与这里包括中国员工在内的所有人面临的艰巨任务相比，我和我的工作毫无意义。我只得等到合适的时间来安排我的事务。同时，我有酒店房间，有饭吃，还有李同志，一刻也没有离开过我；当我在我的房间时，他坐在他的门边，一直观察着我。

I was also well aware that I was but a mote of dust in the face of the vastness that is China and that I, as well as my work, meant nothing when compared to the great tasks facing everyone here, including the staff of Chungkuo, and that I simply had to wait until the time was right for arranging my affairs. Meantime, I had a hotel room, food, and Comrade Li, who did not leave me alone for even a moment; when I was in my room, he sat by the door of his, observing me all the while.

我坐下来读毛泽东著作。这一努力与当时的法令不谋而合：全城都挂着巨幅横幅，上面写着“好好学习毛主席不朽思想”！我当时正在读毛泽东 1935 年 12 月在瓦窑堡召开的党的核心骨干会议上发表的演讲，其中他讨论了长征的影响，“历史上的第一次长征”，因为他说：叫它。 “十二个月来，我们每天都受到数十架飞机从空中的侦察和轰炸，而在陆地上，我们又受到数十万大军的围追堵截，在路上遇到了难以言表的困难和危险。方式;却用两条腿，横扫了十一个省，两万多里的距离。试问，历史上有过与我们相媲美的长征吗？没有永不。”由于这次行军，毛泽东的军队“翻越了终年积雪的山脉和无路可走的草原”，才逃脱了蒋介石的追击，并在后来发动了反攻。

I sat and read the works of Mao Tse-tung. This effort coincided nicely with the decree of the moment: huge banners all over town proclaimed DILIGENTLY STUDY THE IMMORTAL THOUGHTS OF CHAIRMAN MAO! I was reading a lecture delivered by Mao in December of 1935, during a meeting of the Party’s hard core in Wayaopao, in which he discussed the effects of the Long March, “the first of its kind in the annals of history,” as he called it. “For twelve months we were under daily reconnaissance and bombing from the skies by scores of planes, while on land we were encircled and pursued, obstructed and intercepted by a huge force of several hundred thousand men, and we encountered untold difficulties and dangers on the way; yet by using our two legs we swept across a distance of more than twenty thousand li through the length and breadth of eleven provinces. Let us ask, has history ever known a long march to equal ours? No, never.” Thanks to this march, in which Mao’s army “cross[ed] perpetually snow-capped mountains and trackless grasslands,” it escaped the forces of Chiang Kai-shek and was later able to mount a counteroffensive.

有时，读腻了毛泽东的书，我就会拿起庄子的书。庄子是一位热心的道家，他蔑视一切世俗，并以道家大圣惠施为榜样。 “当中国的传奇统治者饶宗颐提出要掌权时，他洗了自己被这种观念玷污的耳朵，避难于奇山荒山。”对于庄子来说，就像对于圣经中的科赫莱一样，外部世界什么也不是，只是虚荣：“与事物冲突或与事物和谐，他们以奔马的速度，无法阻挡，追寻到底； ——这不悲伤吗？一生劳作，不见成果，劳苦劳累，不知往何处去，这不是可悲吗？人们可能会说：“但这不是死亡”；但这有什么好处呢？当身体腐烂时，心灵也会随之腐烂，这难道不是一件非常悲惨的事吗？”

Sometimes, tired of reading Mao, I would pick up Chuang Tzu’s book. Chuang Tzu, a fervent Taoist, scorned all worldliness and held up Hui Shi, a great Taoist sage, as an example. “When Jao, a legendary ruler of China, proposed that he should assume power, he washed his ears, which had been defiled by such a notion, and took refuge on the desolate mountain of K’i-Shan.” For Chuang Tzu, as for the biblical Kohelet, the external world was nothing, mere vanity: “In conflict with things or in harmony with them, they pursue their course to the end, with the speed of a galloping horse which cannot be stopped;—is it not sad? To be constantly toiling all one’s lifetime, without seeing the fruit of one’s labor, and to be weary and worn out with his labor, without knowing where he is going to: is it not a deplorable case? Men may say, ‘But it is not death’; yet of what advantage is this? When the body is decomposed, the mind will be the same along with it: must not the case be pronounced very deplorable?”

庄子被怀疑和不确定所困扰：“言语不仅是呼气。言语是为了传达某种东西，但具体是什么尚未完全确定。是否真的存在类似言语的东西，或者根本就没有类似言语的东西？人们能否将其视为与鸟鸣不同的声音？”

Chuang Tzu is beset by doubts and uncertainties: “Speech is not only the exhaling of air. Speech is meant to convey something, but what that is has not been fully determined. Is there really something like speech, or is there nothing at all like it? Can one see it as distinct from the warbling of birds, or not?”

我想问李同志，中国人会如何解读这些片段，但我担心，在当前的学习毛泽东语录运动中，这些片段听起来可能过于挑衅。所以我选了一些关于蝴蝶的天真的故事：“庄子曾经梦见自己是一只蝴蝶，一只飞来飞去的蝴蝶，对自己感到高兴，为所欲为。他不知道自己是庄子。突然他醒了，他就在那里，坚实而明确无误的庄子。但他不知道自己是庄子梦见自己是蝴蝶，还是蝴蝶梦见自己是庄子。庄子和蝴蝶肯定是有区别的！这就是所谓的事物的转变。”

I wanted to ask Comrade Li how a Chinese would interpret these fragments, but I was afraid that they might sound too provocative in the face of the ongoing campaign to study the sayings of Mao. So I picked something innocent, about a butterfly: “Once Chuang Tzu dreamt he was a butterfly, a butterfly flitting and flittering about, happy with himself and doing as he pleased. He didn’t know he was Chuang Tzu. Suddenly he woke up and there he was, solid and unmistakable Chuang Tzu. But he didn’t know if he was Chuang Tzu who had dreamt he was a butterfly, or a butterfly dreaming he was Chuang Tzu. Between Chuang Tzu and a butterfly there must be some distinction! This is called the Transformation of Things.”

我请李同志给我解释一下这个故事的意义。他听了，微笑着，并仔细地记了下来。他说他得先咨询一下人，然后会给我答案。

I asked Comrade Li to explain the meaning of this story to me. He listened, smiled, and carefully noted it down. He said he would have to consult someone and then would give me the answer.

他从来没有这样做过。

He never did.

•••

•   •   •

我读完《毛泽东》第一卷，开始读第二卷。 1930年代末，日军已占领中国大片领土，并进一步向内地挺进。毛泽东和蒋介石这两个对手结成了战术联盟，以对抗日本侵略者。战争旷日持久，占领者残暴，国家满目疮痍。毛泽东认为，与主要敌人斗争的最佳策略是灵活机动，不断折磨对手。他不断地谈论和写作这一点。

I finished volume one of Mao Tse-tung and started on volume two. It is the end of the 1930s, the Japanese army already occupies a large portion of China and is advancing further into the interior. The two adversaries, Mao Tse-tung and Chiang Kai-shek, enter into a tactical alliance in order to make a stand against the Japanese invader. The war drags on, the occupier is savage, and the country devastated. In Mao’s opinion, the best tactic in the struggle against a prevailing enemy is an adroit elasticity and ceaseless tormenting of the opponent. He speaks and writes about this constantly.

1938年春天，我正在云南读毛泽东关于抗日战争的演讲，李同志在房间里讲完电话后，放下听筒，进来宣布明天我们将去长城。长城！人们从天涯海角赶来观看它。它是世界奇迹之一，是一个独特的、近乎神话般的、在某种意义上深不可测的创造。中国人在两千多年的时间里不断地建造它。当佛陀和希罗多德在世时，他们就开始建造这座建筑，而当列奥纳多·达·芬奇、提香和约翰·塞巴斯蒂安·巴赫在欧洲工作时，他们仍在建造它。

I was reading a lecture about the lengthy war with Japan which Mao delivered in the spring of 1938 in Yunnan when Comrade Li, having finished a telephone conversation in his room, put down the receiver and came in to announce that tomorrow we would be going to the Great Wall. The Great Wall! People come from the ends of the earth to see it. It is one of the wonders of the world, a unique, almost mythical, and in some sense unfathomable creation. The Chinese constructed it, with interruptions, over the course of two thousand years. They commenced when the Buddha and Herodotus were alive and were still building it when Leonardo da Vinci, Titian, and Johann Sebastian Bach were at their labors in Europe.

据不同估计，这堵墙有三到一万公里长。情况各不相同，因为没有单一的长城——而是有多条长城。它们是在不同的时间、不同的地点、用不同的材料建造的。然而，他们有一个共同点：最初的冲动。一个朝代一建立，就立即着手修筑长城。建墙的想法占据了中国统治者的心。如果他们暂时停止建设，那只是因为缺乏资金，一旦他们的财务状况好转，他们就会重新开始建设。

The wall is variously estimated as being from three to ten thousand kilometers long. Variously, because there is no single Great Wall—there are several of them. And they were built at different times, in different places, and from different materials. They had one thing in common, however: the originating impulse. As soon as one dynasty came to power, it immediately set about erecting the Great Wall. The idea of a wall possessed China’s rulers. If they ceased construction for a while, it was only because of a lack of means—they were right back at it the instant their finances improved.

中国人修建长城是为了抵御不安分、扩张主义的蒙古游牧部落的入侵。这些部落以大军、部落、军团的形式，从蒙古大草原、阿尔泰山脉和戈壁沙漠中崛起，攻击中国人，不断威胁他们的国家，以屠杀和奴役的威胁散布恐怖。

The Chinese built the Great Wall to defend against invasions by the restless and expansionist nomadic tribes of Mongolia. These tribes, in great armies, hordes, legions, emerged from the Mongolian steppes, from the Altai mountains and the Gobi desert, and attacked the Chinese, constantly menacing their nation, sowing terror with the threat of slaughter and enslavement.

但长城只是一个隐喻——一个象征和标志，是几千年来这个城墙国家的纹章和盾徽。长城划定了帝国的北部边界。但交战的诸侯国之间、地区之间甚至邻里之间也竖起了围墙。这些建筑保卫着城市和村庄、通道和桥梁。他们守卫宫殿、政府大楼、寺庙和市场。军营、警察局和监狱。围墙包围着私人住宅，将邻居与邻居、家人与家人隔开。如果我们假设中国人数百年甚至数千年不间断地修建城墙，如果考虑到在整个国家历史上数量庞大的人口，他们的奉献精神、模范纪律和蚂蚁般的目标，那么我们可以算出成百上千的人。建造围墙花费了数百万个小时，而在这个贫穷的国家，这些时间本来可以用来学习阅读、获得职业、耕种新田和饲养强壮的牛。

But the Great Wall was only a metaphor—a symbol and a sign, the coat of arms and the escutcheon of what had been a nation of walls for millennia. The Great Wall demarcated the empire’s northern borders; but walls were also erected between warring principalities, between regions and even neighborhoods. The structures defended cities and villages, passes and bridges. They guarded palaces, government buildings, temples, and markets. Barracks, police stations, and prisons. Walls encircled private homes, separated neighbor from neighbor, family from family. If one assumes that the Chinese built walls uninterruptedly for hundreds, even thousands of years, and if one factors in the population—enormous throughout the national history—their dedication and devotion, their exemplary discipline and antlike purposefulness, then one reckons with hundreds upon hundreds of millions of hours spent building walls, hours which in this poor country could have been spent learning to read, acquiring a profession, cultivating new fields, and breeding robust cattle.

世界能源就是这样被浪费的。完全不合理！完全是徒劳！因为长城——它是一座巨大的城墙要塞，绵延数千公里，穿过无人居住的山脉和荒野，是令人自豪的对象，正如我已经提到的，它是世界奇迹之一——也证明了一种人性的弱点，一种失常，一种可怕的错误；这是地球这一地区的人们历史上无法沟通、协商和共同决定的证据如何最好地利用人类巨大的能量和智力储备。

That is how the world’s energy is wasted. In complete irrationality! Complete futility! For the Great Wall—and it is gigantic, a wall-fortress, stretching for thousands of kilometers through uninhabited mountains and wilderness, an object of pride and, as I have mentioned, one of the wonders of the world—is also proof of a kind of human weakness, of an aberration, of a horrifying mistake; it is evidence of a historical inability of people in this part of the planet to communicate, to confer and jointly determine how best to deploy enormous reserves of human energy and intellect.

在这些地方，团结起来的想法只是一个幻想：面对潜在麻烦的第一反应就是建造一堵墙。要把自己封闭起来，把自己围起来。因为无论来自外面、那边的任何东西，都只能是威胁、不幸的预兆、邪恶的预兆——也许是最真实的邪恶。

In these parts, the idea of coming together was but a chimera: The very first reflex in the face of potential trouble was to build a wall. To shut oneself in, fence oneself off. Because whatever comes from without, from over there, can only be a threat, an omen of misfortune, a harbinger of evil—perhaps the most genuine evil there is.

修建隔离墙的动机不仅仅是出于外部考虑。在防范外国威胁的同时，它还允许人们控制内部发生的事情。城墙上有通道，有门有门，有人把守，当然可以控制谁进谁出。人们可以提问，人们可以检查有效文件，人们可以记下名字，看面孔，观察，牢记记忆。因此，这样的墙同时是盾牌和陷阱，面纱和笼子。

And the wall is not merely motivated by exterior considerations. Protecting against foreign menaces, it also allows one to control what is happening internally. There are passages in the wall, doors and gates, and guarding them, of course, one could control who entered and exited. One could question, one could check for valid papers, one could take down names, look at faces, observe, commit to memory. And thus such a wall is simultaneously a shield and a trap, a veil and a cage.

围墙最糟糕的一面是让这么多人变成它的捍卫者，并产生一种心态，认为围墙贯穿一切，想象世界被分为外部邪恶和低等的部分，以及善良和优越的部分。部分，在里面。隔离墙的守护者无需亲自靠近隔离墙；他可以在很远的地方，只要他内心携带着墙的形象并宣誓效忠墙所规定的逻辑原则就足够了。

The worst aspect of the wall is to turn so many people into its defenders and produce a mental attitude that sees a wall running through everything, imagines the world as being divided into an evil and inferior part, on the outside, and a good and superior part, on the inside. A keeper of the wall need not be in physical proximity to it; he can be far away and it is enough that he carry within himself its image and pledge allegiance to the logical principles that the wall dictates.

长城位于北京以北一小时车程处。首先，我们穿过城市的部分地区。一阵冰冷的风吹来。行人和骑自行车的人向前倾身，与大风搏斗。到处都是骑自行车的人。当灯光变红时，每条河流都会停止流动，就像突然关闭的船闸一样，然后恢复流动，直到下一组灯光亮起。只有风能扰乱这种原本单调、费力的节奏：如果流速太猛烈，河水就会开始汹涌澎湃，使一些骑自行车的人旋转，迫使其他人停下来下车。队伍中爆发出混乱和混乱。但风一停，一切又会回到原来的位置，尽职尽责地向前推进。

The Great Wall is one hour’s drive north of Peking. At first, we pass through parts of the city. An ice-cold wind is blowing. Pedestrians and bicyclists lean forward, struggling with the gale. There are rivers of bicyclists everywhere. Each of these rivers halts when the lights turn red, as if a lock had suddenly been closed, then resumes its flow until the next set of lights. Only the wind disrupts this otherwise monotonous, laborious rhythm: If it picks up too violently, the river begins to surge and billow, spinning some bicyclists around and forcing others to stop and dismount. Confusion and chaos erupt in the ranks. But as soon as the wind subsides, everything continues once again in its proper place and dutiful movement forward.

市中心的人行道上挤满了人，经常可以看到一排排穿着校服的小学生。他们成双成对地走着，挥舞着小红旗，走在最前面的人要么拿着红旗，要么拿着好叔叔毛主席的肖像。孩子们热情地叫着、唱着、或者齐声喊叫。他们在说什么？我问李同志。 “他们想学习毛主席的思想，”他回答道。每个角落都能看到警察，他们总是给这些游行队伍让路。

The sidewalks in the center of the city are full of people and one frequently sees columns of schoolchildren clad in school uniforms. They walk in pairs waving little red flags, and the one at the head of the procession carries either a red banner or a portrait of the Good Uncle—Chairman Mao. The children enthusiastically call, sing, or cry out in unison. What are they saying? I ask Comrade Li. “They want to study the thoughts of Chairman Mao,” he replies. The policemen, whom one sees on every corner, always give these processions the right-of-way.

整个城市都是黄色和海军蓝色的。街道前面的建筑物是黄色的，每个人穿的衣服都是海军蓝的。 “这些制服是革命的成果，”李同志解释道。 “以前，人们没有衣服穿，就会被冻死。”男人的发型就像新兵一样，而女人，无论是女孩还是老太太，都留着短的花童式刘海。人们必须仔细观察才能将一个人与另一个人区分开来——这是一种尴尬，因为凝视被认为是不礼貌的。

The city is all yellow and navy blue. The buildings fronting the streets are yellow and the clothes everyone wears are navy. “These uniforms are an achievement of the Revolution,” explains Comrade Li. “Before, people had nothing to wear and died of cold.” Men have their hair cut like military recruits, and women, be they girls or old ladies, wear theirs in a short pageboy style with bangs. One has to look closely to distinguish one individual from another—an awkwardness, since it is considered impolite to stare.

如果有人拿着一个包，那么这个包和其他包是一样的。当有大型聚会并且每个人都必须将帽子和包放在衣帽间时会发生什么？他们如何将自己的物品与成千上万其他人的物品区分开来？我不知道——但他们似乎是这么做的。这证明真正的差异不仅存在于大的事物中，而且存在于最小的细节中——例如纽扣的缝制方式。

If someone is carrying a bag, then that bag is identical to all the rest. What happens when there is a large gathering and everyone must leave their caps and bags in a cloakroom? How do they distinguish their belongings from those of thousands of others? I have no idea—and yet they appear to do so. It is proof that real differences can indeed dwell not only in large things, but in the smallest of details—in the way, for instance, that a button has been sewn on.

人们通过其中一座废弃的塔楼登上长城。城墙上布满了巨大的垛口和塔楼，其宽度足以容纳十个人并排行走。从我们的有利位置来看，墙蜿蜒延伸至无限远，每一端都消失在山脉和森林之外的某个地方。这里荒无人烟，周围没有人影，风撕扯着我们。我将这一切尽收眼底，触摸了几个世纪前人们因精疲力尽而拖到这里的巨石。为了什么目的？这有什么意义呢？它有什么用呢？

One mounts the Great Wall through one of its abandoned towers. The wall is bristling with massive crenellations and turrets, and wide enough for ten people to walk along it side by side. From our vantage point, the wall serpentines into infinity, each end disappearing somewhere beyond mountains and forests. It is deserted, not a soul around, and the wind tears at us. I take it all in, touch the boulders dragged here centuries ago by people dropping from exhaustion. To what end? What sense does it make? Of what use is it?

随着时间的推移，我越来越将长城视为伟大的隐喻。我周围都是无法交流的人，周围都是我无法理解的世界。我本来应该写的——但是写什么呢？报纸上全是中文，所以我什么也听不懂。起初我请李同志给我翻译，但他翻译的每一篇文章都是这样开头的：“正如毛主席教导我们的那样”，“按照毛主席的建议”等等，等等。实际上是写的吗？我与外界唯一的联系就是李同志，他是最难以逾越的障碍。对于我每次见面、谈话、旅行的要求，他都会回答：“我会把这个转达给报纸。”我不会再听到任何关于此事的消息。没有李同志，我也不能单独出去。但我又能去哪里呢？去见谁？我不认识这个城市，我不认识任何人，我没有电话（只有李同志有一部）。

With each passing day I thought of the Great Wall more and more as the Great Metaphor. I was surrounded by people with whom I could not communicate, encircled by a world I could not fathom. I was supposed to write—but about what? The press was exclusively in Chinese, so I understood nothing of it. At first I asked Comrade Li to translate for me, but every article, in his translation, began with the words: “As Chairman Mao teaches us,” or “Following the recommendations of Chairman Mao,” etc., etc. Is that what was actually written? My only link to the outside world was Comrade Li, and he was the most impenetrable barrier of all. To my every request for a meeting, a conversation, a trip, he responded, “I will convey this to the newspaper.” And I would hear nothing more on the matter. Nor could I go out alone, without Comrade Li. But where could I have gone anyway? To see whom? I did not know the city, I knew no one, I had no telephone (only Comrade Li had one).

最重要的是，我不懂这种语言。是的，我确实从一开始就尝试过研究它。我试图在象形文字和表意文字的丛林中撕开一条路，结果却遇到了每个字符令人发狂的多重含义的死胡同。我刚刚在某处读到，存在八十多个《道德经》（道教圣经）的英文译本，全部都是合格且可靠的——而且全然不同！我的双腿在我身下弯曲。不，我心想，我无法应付这个，我无法应付。这些字符在我眼前闪烁，闪烁着脉动，改变着形状和位置、关系和联系、比例和图案；乘除，成行成列，交换位置，“瓯”字里不知怎么出现了“ao”字形，或者突然把“eng”字和“ong”字混淆了——真是一个可怕的错误。

Above all, I did not know the language. Yes, I did try studying it, right from the start. I attempted to tear my way through the thickets of hieroglyphs and ideograms only to come up against the dead end of each character’s maddening multiplicity of meanings. I had just read somewhere that there exist more than eighty English translations of the Tao Te Ching (the bible of Taoism), all of them competent and reliable—and all utterly different! My legs buckled beneath me. No, I thought to myself, I cannot cope with this, I cannot manage. The characters flickered before my eyes, shimmered and pulsated, changed shape and position, relations and connections, proportions and patterns; they multiplied and divided, formed rows and columns, exchanged places, the shapes for “ao” appeared who knows how in the character for “ou,” or suddenly I confused the notation for “eng” with the notation for “ong”—which was a truly horrendous error.

中国思想

CHINESE THOUGHT

我我手头有很多时间，大部分时间都花在阅读在香港购买的有关中国的书籍上。它们是如此引人入胜，以至于我会暂时忘记希罗多德和希腊人。

I had a lot of time on my hands and spent much of it reading the books about China which I had purchased in Hong Kong. They were so absorbing that I would momentarily forget about Herodotus and the Greeks.

我仍然相信我会在这里工作，因此想尽可能多地了解这个国家及其人民。我没有意识到大多数报道中国的记者都在香港、东京或首尔，他们要么是中国人，要么至少能说流利的语言，而我在北京的处境有些不可能和不真实。 。

I still believed that I would be working here, and therefore wanted to learn as much as possible about this country and its people. I didn’t realize that the majority of correspondents reporting on China were based in Hong Kong, Tokyo, or Seoul, that they were either Chinese or at least fluent in the language, and that there was something impossible and unreal about my situation in Peking.

我时时感受到长城的存在；这不是我几天前在北方山区看到的那座，而是对我来说更可怕、更难以逾越的那座——语言长城。我多么渴望自己的目光能够落在某个可辨认的字母或表情上，抓住它，松一口气，有宾至如归的感觉。一切都是徒劳。一切都难以辨认、晦涩难懂、难以捉摸。

I constantly felt the presence of the Great Wall; not the one I had seen several days ago in the mountains to the north, but the much more formidable and insurmountable one for me—the Great Wall of Language. How desperately I yearned for my gaze to alight on some recognizable letter or expression, to hold on to it, breathe a sigh of relief, feel at home. All in vain. Everything was illegible, obscure, inscrutable.

这实际上与我在印度的感受没有什么不同。在那里我也无法理解当地印度教字母的丛林。如果我再走得更远，会不会遇到类似的障碍？

It was actually not dissimilar to how I had felt in India. There too I could not penetrate the thicket of the local Hindu alphabet. And were I to travel farther still, would I not encounter similar barriers?

这座按语言字母顺序排列的巴别塔到底是从哪里来的呢？特定的字母表是如何出现的？在某个原始点，在一开始，它必须从一个符号、一个字符开始。有人为了记住某事而做了记号。或者与别人交流某事。或者对一个物体或一个领土施展咒语。

Where did this linguistic-alphabetical Tower of Babel come from, anyway? How does a particular alphabet arise? At some primal point, at the very beginning, it had to start with a single sign, a single character. Someone made a mark in order to remember something. Or to communicate something to someone else. Or to cast a spell on an object or a territory.

但为什么不同的人会用这么多完全不同的符号来描述同一个物体呢？在世界各地，一个人、一座山或一棵树看起来都很相似，但在每个字母表中，都有不同的符号、图像或字母与之相对应。为什么第一个想要描述花朵的人在一种文化中画了一条垂直线，在另一种文化中画了一个圆圈，而在第三种文化中决定画两条线和一个圆锥体？这些第一批涂鸦者是自己做出这些决定的，还是集体做出的？他们事先商量过吗？晚上围着火讨论它们？在家庭理事会期间请求认可？在部落聚会上？他们有没有征求长辈的意见？来自江湖骗子？来自占卜者？

But why do different people describe the same object with so many completely different notations? All over the world a man, a mountain, or a tree look much alike, and yet in each alphabet different symbols, images, or letters correspond to them. Why is it that the very first individual who wanted to describe a flower made a vertical line in one culture, a circle in another culture, and in a third decided on two lines and a cone? Did these first scribblers make these decisions on their own, or collectively? Did they talk them over beforehand? Discuss them around the fire at night? Request endorsement during a family council? At a tribal gathering? Did they seek counsel from the elders? From charlatans? From soothsayers?

如果知道的话就好了，因为一旦骰子掷出，就无法回头。事情有自己的动力。从第一个最简单的决定开始——向左画一条线，向右画一条线——其余的一切都会随之而来，变得越来越巧妙和复杂，因为根据字母表的恶魔进化逻辑，随着时间的推移，字母表变得越来越复杂，越来越少，越来越复杂。对于外行来说不太容易辨认，甚至最终变得完全无法辨认，就像不止一次发生的那样。

It would be good to know, because later, once the die has been cast, one cannot turn back. Matters acquire their own momentum. From that first, simplest decision—to make one line to the left and one to the right—all the rest will follow, increasingly ingenious and intricate, because by the alphabet’s fiendish evolutionary logic the alphabet with time grows more and more complex, less and less legible to the uninitiated, even to the point of finally becoming, as has occurred more than once, utterly indecipherable.

尽管印地语和中文书写系统给我带来了同样的困难，但两国人民的行为却截然不同。印度教徒是一个轻松的人，而中国人是一个紧张而警惕的人。一群印度教徒是无形的、流动的、缓慢的；不知不觉间，一群中国人就已经排成了有纪律的行军队伍。人们会感觉到，在一群中国人之上矗立着一位指挥官，一个更高的权威，而在众多印度教徒之上，则盘旋着无数且要求不高的神祇。如果一群印度教徒遇到一些有趣的事情，他们就会停下来，看看，然后开始讨论。在类似的情况下，中国人也会排成紧密的队形，听话地走下去，眼睛盯着指定的目标。印度教徒明显更加仪式化、神秘化、宗教化。在印度，精神领域及其象征总是触手可及、触手可及、触手可及。圣人行路；朝圣者前往寺庙，众神的所在地；群众聚集在圣山脚下，在圣河中沐浴，在圣火堆上火化死者。中国人在精神上显得不那么张扬，明显更加谨慎和封闭。他们不去祭拜神灵，而是注重遵守适当的礼仪；道路上行进的不是圣人，而是作品。

Although the Hindi and the Chinese writing systems caused me equal difficulty, the behavior of people in the two countries could not have been more different. The Hindu is a relaxed being, while the Chinese is a tense and vigilant one. A crowd of Hindus is formless, fluid, slow; a crowd of Chinese is formed before you know it into disciplined marching lines. One senses that above a gathering of Chinese stands a commander, a higher authority, while above the multitude of Hindus hovers an Areopagus of innumerable and undemanding deities. If a throng of Hindus encounters something interesting, it stops, looks, and begins discussing. In a similar situation, the Chinese will walk on, in close formation, obedient, their eyes fixed on a designated goal. The Hindus are significantly more ritualistic, mystical, religious. The realm of the spirit and its symbols is always close at hand in India, present, perceptible. Holy men wander along the roads; pilgrimages head for temples, the seats of the gods; masses gather at the feet of holy mountains, bathe in holy rivers, cremate the dead on holy pyres. The Chinese appear spiritually less ostentatious, significantly more discreet and closed. Instead of paying homage to gods, they concern themselves with observing proper etiquette; instead of holy men, works march along the roads.

我发现他们的脸也不同。印度教徒的脸上充满惊讶；额头上的红点，脸颊上的彩色图案，或者微笑时露出深棕色的牙齿。中国人的脸上没有这样的惊喜。它是光滑的并且具有不变的特征。似乎没有什么可以扰乱其平静的表面。这张脸传达出它隐藏着一些我们一无所知、也永远不会知道的东西。

Their faces, too, I found are different. The face of a Hindu contains surprise; a red dot on a forehead, colorful patterns on cheeks, or a smile that reveals teeth stained dark brown. The face of a Chinese holds no such surprises. It is smooth and has unvarying features. It seems as if nothing could ruffle its still surface. It is a face that communicates that it is hiding something about which we know nothing and never will.

有一次李同志带我去上海。和北京有什么区别啊！这座城市的巨大和建筑的多样性令我震惊——整个街区都是法国风格、意大利风格或美国风格建造的。绵延数公里的林荫大道、林荫大道、海滨长廊、拱廊随处可见。城市发展的规模和活力、大都市的喧嚣、汽车、人力车、无数的行人。许多商店，甚至偶尔还有酒吧。这里比北京暖和得多，空气也很温和，让人感觉离大海很近。

One time Comrade Li took me to Shanghai. What a difference from Peking! I was stunned by the immensity of this city, by the diversity of its architecture—entire neighborhoods built in the French style, or the Italian, or the American. Everywhere, for kilometers on end, shaded avenues, boulevards, promenades, arcades. The scale and energy of urban development, the metropolitan bustle, the cars, the rickshaws, the untold multitudes of pedestrians. Many stores and even the occasional bar. It is much warmer here than in Peking and the air is gentle—one senses the proximity of the sea.

有一天，当我们开车经过一个日本社区时，我注意到一座佛教寺庙的沉重、矮胖的柱子。 “这座寺庙还开门吗？”我问李同志。 “在这里，在上海，当然是这样，”他回答道，语气中夹杂着讽刺和蔑视，仿佛上海是中国，但不是百分百如此，也不完全是毛泽东所说的中国。

As we drove one day through a Japanese neighborhood, I noticed the heavy, squat columns of a Buddhist temple. “Is this temple open?” I asked Comrade Li. “Here, in Shanghai, certainly so,” he answered, with a mixture of irony and scorn, as if Shanghai were China but not 100 percent so, not fully a China according to Mao Tse-tung.

佛教直到本世纪第一个千年才在中国盛行。在此之前的大约五百年里，两种平行的精神潮流、两种学派、两种取向主导着该地区：儒教和道教。孔子大师生活于公元前560 年至 480 年。对于道教的创始人老子是否比孔子年长或年轻，历史学家们并没有达成共识。许多学者甚至认为老子根本不存在，据说他留下的唯一一本小书——《道德经》——只不过是由匿名抄写员收集的片段、警句和俗语的集合。抄写员。

Buddhism did not flower in China until the first millennium of our era. For some five hundred years prior to that time, two parallel spiritual currents, two schools, two orientations dominated the region: Confucianism and Taoism. Master Confucius lived from 560 to 480 B.C.E. There is no consensus among historians as to whether the creator of Taoism—Master Lao-tzu—was older or younger than Confucius. Many scholars even maintain that Lao-tzu did not exist at all, and the only little book which he is said to have left behind him—the Tao Te Ching—is simply a collection of fragments, aphorisms, and sayings gathered by anonymous scribes and copyists.

如果我们承认老子确实存在并且比孔子年长，那么我们也可以相信这个经常被重复的故事，即年轻的孔子如何前往智者老子居住的地方，并向他请教如何做事。引导他的生活。 ”老人回答说：“去掉傲慢和欲望，去掉阿谀奉承和过度野心的习惯。所有这些都会给你带来伤害。这就是我要对你说的一切。”

If we accept that Lao-tzu did exist and was older than Confucius, then we can also believe the story, often repeated, about how young Confucius made a journey to where the wise man Lao-tzu lived and asked him for advice on how to conduct his life. “Rid yourself of arrogance and desire,” the old man answered, “rid yourself of the habit of flattery and of excessive ambition. All this causes you harm. That is all that I have to say to you.”

但如果是比老子年长的孔子，那么他可以将这三点传给他的年轻同胞。伟大的想法。第一：“如果你不知道如何侍奉人，你怎么知道如何侍奉神呢？”第二：“为什么要以善报恶呢？那你要怎样回报呢？第三：“在你了解生者之前，你如何了解死者？”

But if it was Confucius who was older than Lao-tzu, then he could have passed on to his younger countryman these three great thoughts. The first: “How can you know how to serve gods if you do not know how to serve people?” The second: “Why do you pay back evil with good? How then will you pay back good?” And third: “Till you know about the living, how are you to know about the dead?”

孔子和老子（如果他确实存在的话）的哲学产生于周朝的暮年，大约在战国时代，当时中国四分五裂，分裂成许多国家，发动了激烈的、人口大量减少的战争。与彼此。一个暂时逃离大屠杀的人仍然被明天的不确定性和恐惧所困扰，他不得不问自己：一个人如何生存？这是中国思想试图回答的问题。这也许是世界上迄今为止最实用的哲学。与印度教思想相反，它很少冒险进入超越的领域，而是试图为普通人提供有关忍受他自己所处处境的建议，原因很简单，在没有他的意愿或同意的情况下，他出生在我们这个残酷的世界。

The philosophies of Confucius and of Lao-tzu (if indeed he existed) arose in the twilight of the Chou dynasty, at around the Epoch of the Warring Kingdoms, when China was torn asunder, divided into numerous states waging fierce, population-decimating war with one another. A man who managed momentarily to escape the carnage is still haunted by uncertainty and fear of tomorrow, and perforce asks himself: How does one survive? This is the question that Chinese thought attempts to answer. It is perhaps the most practical philosophy the world has ever known. In contrast to Hindu thought, it rarely ventures into the realms of transcendence, and tries instead to offer the ordinary man advice on enduring the situation in which he finds himself for the simple reason that, without either his will or consent, he was born into this cruel world of ours.

正是在这一点上，孔子和老子（如果存在的话）的道路出现了分歧，或者更准确地说，对于最基本的世俗问题——“我如何生存？”——他们各自给出了不同的答案。孔子认为，人诞生于社会，就负有一定的义务。最重要的是执行当局的命令和服从父母。另外——尊重祖先和传统；严格遵守礼仪规则；忠于现有秩序；和对改变的抵制。儒家的人对于当权者是忠诚而温顺的。大师说，如果你服从并认真地遵守他们的指示，你就会生存下来。

It is at this point that the paths of Confucius and Lao-tzu (if he existed) diverge, or, more precisely, it is to the most fundamental of worldly questions—“How do I survive?”—that each gives a different answer. Confucius holds that man, being born into society, has certain obligations. The most important are those of carrying out the commands of the authorities and submissiveness to one’s parents. Also—respect for ancestors and tradition; the strict observance of the rules of etiquette; fealty to the existing order; and resistance to change. The Confucian man is loyal and docile vis-à-vis those in power. If you obediently and conscientiously hew to their dictates, says the master, you will survive.

老子（如果他存在的话）建议采取不同的立场。这道教创始人建议远离一切。大师说，没有什么是永恒的。所以不要执着于任何事物。一切存在的事物都会消亡；因此，要超越它，保持距离，不要试图成为某个人，不要试图追求或拥有某些东西。以无为为：你的强项是软弱和无助；你的智慧、天真和无知。如果你想生存，就变得无用，对每个人来说都是不必要的。远离他人，做隐士，吃一碗饭，喝一口水就满足了。最重要的是——遵守道。但什么是道呢？这是不可能的，因为道的本质是它的模糊性和不可表达性：“如果道让自己被定义为道，那么它就不是真正的道，”大师说。道是一条路，不是一个方向，守道就是沿着这条路一直走下去。

Lao-tzu (if he existed) recommends a different stance. The creator of Taoism advises keeping oneself at a remove from everything. Nothing lasts, says the master. So do not become attached to anything. All that exists will perish; therefore rise above it, maintain your distance, do not try to become somebody, do not try to pursue or possess something. Act through inaction: your strength is weakness and helplessness; your wisdom, naïveté and ignorance. If you want to survive, become useless, unnecessary to everyone. Live far from others, become a hermit, be satisfied with a bowl of rice, a sip of water. And most important—observe the Tao. But what is Tao? It’s impossible to say, because the essence of Tao is its vagueness and inexpressibleness: “If Tao lets itself be defined as Tao, then it is not genuine Tao,” says the master. Tao is a path, not a heading, and to observe Tao is to keep to that path and walk straight ahead.

儒家思想是关于权力、官僚、结构、秩序和立正的哲学。道家是放弃游戏的智慧，是安于自己只是一个无足轻重的自然微粒的智慧。

Confucianism is the philosophy of power, of bureaucrats, of structure, order, and of standing at attention; Taoism is the wisdom of renouncing the game, of contenting oneself with being only an insignificant particle of indifferent nature.

然而，儒家和道家向简单人传达的信息有一个共同点：提倡谦逊。有趣的是，大约在同一时间，也在亚洲，出现了另外两种知识学科：佛教和爱奥尼亚哲学，它们为普通人提供了相同的建议：保持谦虚。

In their message to the simple man, however, Confucianism and Taoism have a common denominator: the recommendation of humility. It is interesting that at approximately the same time, and also in Asia, arise two other intellectual disciplines, Buddhism and Ionian philosophy, which offer lesser mortals the identical advice: be humble.

儒家艺术家的绘画描绘了宫廷场景——坐着的皇帝，周围是僵硬的站着的官僚、宫廷礼宾长官、威严的将军、温顺鞠躬的仆人。在道家画中，我们看到远处的粉彩风景，难以辨认的山脉，发光的薄雾，桑树，以及前景中细长的竹叶，在无形的微风中摇曳。

The paintings of Confucian artists depict court scenes—a seated emperor surrounded by stiff standing bureaucrats, chiefs of palace protocol, pompous generals, meekly bowing servants. In Taoist paintings we see distant pastel landscapes, barely discernible mountain chains, luminous mists, mulberry trees, and in the foreground a slender, delicate leaf of a bamboo bush, swaying in the invisible breeze.

我和李同志一起漫步在上海的街头，观察过往的行人，我现在问自己，他们是儒家、道家还是佛家。

Strolling with Comrade Li along the streets of Shanghai and observing the passersby, I now ask myself whether each is a Confucian, a Taoist, or a Buddhist.

但这是一种毫无意义的好奇立场。因为中国哲学的强大之处在于它灵活而统一的融合性，即不同的趋势、观点和立场融合成一个整体，同时又不损害各个思想流派的核心完整性。在中国数千年的历史进程中，许多不同的哲学（很难将它们称为欧洲意义上的宗教，因为它们不包括上帝的概念）占据主导地位——儒家思想占主导地位，或者道家思想占主导地位，最著名的是佛教；他们之间时不时会出现冲突或紧张；有时，皇帝会支持一种或另一种精神潮流，有时促进它们的共存，有时则煽动它们之间的竞争和冲突。但迟早会出现某种程度的妥协、相互渗透、一致。如此多的东西落入这个文明历史的巨大鸿沟，被它吸收，随后以明显的中国形状和特征出现。

But this is a pointlessly inquisitive stance. For the great strength of Chinese philosophy is its flexible and unifying syncretism, the way varied trends, views, and positions merge into a single whole while in no way jeopardizing the core integrity of each separate school of thought. In the course of thousands of years of Chinese history, many and different philosophies (it is difficult to call them religions in the European sense of that word, since they do not include the concept of God) held sway—Confucianism prevailed, or Taoism, or Buddhism, to name the most prominent; now and then a conflict or tension would arise among them; occasionally an emperor would throw his support behind one or another of the spiritual trends, at times fostering their coexistence, at other times inciting competition and strife among them. But sooner or later there would be compromise, interpenetration, accord of one kind or another. So much fell into the immense chasm of this civilization’s history, was absorbed by it, subsequently to emerge with an unmistakably Chinese shape and character.

这种综合的变革过程也可能发生在中国人个体的灵魂中。根据情况、背景和环境，儒家因素可能在他或道家身上占上风，因为在他的世界里，没有什么是一劳永逸、签字盖章、写在石头上的。为了生存，他要做一个听话的执行者。外表谦逊、温顺，内心却冷漠、遥不可及、独立。

This synthetic transformative process could also occur in the soul of the individual Chinese. Depending on the situation, the context, and the circumstances, the Confucian element might take the upper hand in him, or the Taoist, because nothing in his world was determined once and for all, signed and sealed, written in stone. To survive, he would be an obedient executor. Humble and meek on the outside, he would as well be on the inside aloof, unreachable, independent.

我们回到北京，回到酒店。我回到我的书本上。我开始研究九世纪伟大诗人韩愈的生平。在有一点，孔子的追随者韩愈开始反对佛教在中国的影响，理由是佛教是外来的印度教意识形态。他撰写批评文章和热情洋溢的小册子。这位伟大诗人的沙文主义激怒了信仰佛教的统治皇帝，他判处韩愈死刑，然后在朝臣的安抚下，改判流放到今天鳄鱼出没的广东省。

We returned to Peking and our hotel. I went back to my books. I began studying the life of the great ninth century poet, Han Yü. At one point Han Yü, a follower of Confucius, begins to combat the influences of Buddhism in China, on the grounds of its being a foreign Hindu ideology. He pens critical essays, fiery pamphlets. The great poet’s chauvinism so angered the ruling emperor, an adherent of Buddhism, that he condemned Han Yü to death and then, propitiated by his courtiers, changed the sentence to exile in what is today the province of Kwangtung, a place infested with crocodiles.

还没等我弄清楚接下来发生的事情， 《中国》编辑部就有人来了，带来了一位来自国际贸易总部的绅士，他又递给我一封我在华沙Sztandar Młodych的同事写的信。因为我们班子公开反对他们写的《Po Prostu》被关闭，所以该报的整个编辑部都被中央撤掉了，该报现在由三位特派员领导。一些记者辞职以示抗议，而另一些记者则犹豫不决，等待着结果。我要做什么，我的朋友们想知道。

Before I was able to find out what happened next, someone arrived from the editorial offices of Chungkuo bringing with him a gentleman from the headquarters of international trade, who in turn handed me a letter from my colleagues at Sztandar Młodych in Warsaw. Because our team had spoken out against the closing of “Po prostu” they wrote, the newspaper’s entire editorial board had been removed by the Central Committee and the paper was now under the direction of three specially appointed commissioners. Some of the journalists had resigned in protest, while others were hesitating, waiting it out. What was I going to do, my friends wanted to know.

国贸部的先生走了，我想都没想就告诉李同志，我接到紧急回国的命令。我会立即开始收拾行李。李同志的脸没有丝毫抽搐。我们互相看了一会儿，然后下楼去了餐厅，晚餐在那里等着我们。

The gentleman from the international trade department left, and without giving it a second’s thought I informed Comrade Li that I had received urgent orders to return home. I would start packing right away. Comrade Li’s face didn’t so much as twitch. We looked at each other for a moment, then went downstairs to the dining room, where dinner awaited us.

我离开中国就像离开印度一样，带着一种失落甚至悲伤的感觉。但与此同时，我的飞行也是有目的的。我必须逃离，因为一个全新的、迄今为止陌生的世界正在将我拉入它的轨道，完全吸引我，让我着迷，压倒我。我立刻被一种深刻的感觉所吸引着迷，对学习的强烈渴望，让自己完全沉浸其中，融化，与这个陌生的宇宙合而为一。知道它就好像我在那里出生、长大、开始生活一样。我想学习语言，我想读书，我想渗透每一个角落。

I was leaving China, as I had India, with a feeling of loss, even of sorrow; but at the same time there was something purposeful about my flight. I had to escape, because a new, hitherto unfamiliar world was pulling me into its orbit, completely absorbing me, obsessing and overwhelming me. I was seized at once with a profound fascination, a burning thirst to learn, to immerse myself totally, to melt away, to become as one with this foreign universe. To know it as if I had been born and raised there, begun life there. I wanted to learn the language, I wanted to read the books, I wanted to penetrate every nook and cranny.

这是一种弊病，一种危险的弱点，因为我也意识到这些文明是如此巨大、如此丰富、复杂和多样，以至于要了解其中的一个片段，哪怕只是一小部分，都需要付出一个人的努力。为企业奉献一生。文化是一座拥有无数房间、走廊、阳台和阁楼的大厦，所有这些都被布置成如此扭曲、旋转的迷宫，如果你进入其中之一，就没有出口、没有退路、没有回头路。成为一名印度教学者、汉学家、阿拉伯学家或希伯来学家是一项崇高的、全身心投入的追求，没有时间或空间去做其他事情。

It was a kind of malady, a dangerous weakness, because I also realized that these civilizations are so enormous, so rich, complex, and varied, that getting to know even a fragment of one of them, a mere scrap, would require devoting one’s whole life to the enterprise. Cultures are edifices with countless rooms, corridors, balconies, and attics, all arranged, furthermore, into such twisting, turning labyrinths, that if you enter one of them, there is no exit, no retreat, no turning back. To become a Hindu scholar, a Sinologist, an Arabist, or a Hebraist is a lofty, all-consuming pursuit, leaving no space or time for anything else.

尽管我有屈服于这种诱惑的冲动，但我也仍然被他们各自世界之外的事物所吸引——我被尚未遇见的人、尚未走过的道路、尚未见过的天空所诱惑。跨越边界、看看边界之外的事物的愿望仍然在我心中激荡。

Whereas I had the urge to submit to such seductions, I also remained attracted to what lay beyond the confines of their respective worlds—I was tempted by people still unmet, roads yet untraveled, skies yet unseen. The desire to cross the border, to look at what is beyond it, stirred in me still.

我回到了华沙。我在中国的奇怪处境、我缺乏真正的目标、我毫无意义地悬浮在真空中的原因很快就变得清晰起来。派我去中国的想法是在两次解冻之后产生的：1956 年 10 月在波兰的解冻，以及在中国毛主席的《百花齐放》的解冻。甚至在我到达中国之前，华沙和北京就已经发生了剧变。波兰共产党领导人瓦迪斯瓦夫·哥穆尔卡发起了一场反对自由派的运动，而毛泽东则发起了严厉的大跃进政治。

I returned to Warsaw. The reasons for my bizarre situation in China, my lack of real purpose, my senseless suspension in a vacuum, quickly became clear. The idea of sending me to China arose in the aftermath of two thaws: that of October 1956 in Poland, and in China, that of Chairman Mao’s One Hundred Flowers. Even before I arrived in China, an upheaval was under way in Warsaw and in Peking. The head of the Polish Communist Party, Władyslaw Gomułka, initiated a campaign against the liberals, and Mao Tse-tung was launching the draconian politics of the Great Leap Forward.

实际上，我应该在到达北京的第二天就离开北京。但我的报纸却表现得沉默寡言——因为恐惧而为生存而奋斗，它已经忘记了我。或者也许编辑们考虑到了我的利益——也许他们认为我在中国会安全？无论如何，我现在认为《中国报》的编辑们已经从中国驻华沙大使馆获悉，斯坦达尔·姆沃迪奇的记者是一份命悬一线的报纸的特使，它被归还只是时间问题。斧头。我还认为，正是中国人热情好客的传统原则、中国人对面子的重视以及他们高度培养的礼貌，使我没有被立即驱逐出境。相反，他们创造了条件，他们认为这些条件会让我猜测，先前商定的合作模式将不再获得。我会自愿地说：我要离开。
